      1 -- Rename Phase ‚Üí Cluster (D/B: "clustering of cues")
      2 ALTER TABLE phase_memberships RENAME TO cluster_memberships;
      3 ALTER TABLE cluster_memberships RENAME COLUMN phase_id TO cluster

      4 ALTER INDEX idx_pm_phase RENAME TO idx_cm_cluster;
      5 ALTER INDEX idx_pm_naming RENAME TO idx_cm_naming;
      6 ALTER INDEX idx_pm_phase_seq RENAME TO idx_cm_cluster_seq;

  Die NamingNets-Memory (project_naming_nets.md) sagt es explizit: "Useful
  beyond import: researchers may want to group namings into thematic clusters,
  code families, etc." ‚ÄĒ Clusters sind NamingNets.

  Das strukturelle Problem f√ľr die Coding-Integration: Clusters sind aktuell an
  eine Map gebunden (parentMapId in appearance properties, participation mit
  mapId). F√ľr den Coding-Kontext brauchen sie einen projektweiten Anker. Der
  existiert schon: das Grounding Workspace (getOrCreateGroundingWorkspace).

  Designvorschlag ‚ÄĒ zwei Ebenen:

  1. Namings-Seite (/namings) ‚ÄĒ der nat√ľrliche Ort f√ľr Cluster-Management:
    - Cluster-Badges an jedem Naming (farbiger Dot + Label)
    - "Group by Cluster" als Gruppierungsoption (wie auf Maps schon
  implementiert)
    - Mehrfachselektion ‚Üí "Create Cluster" (benennen, Designation =
  characterization)
    - Cluster-Sidebar oder -Section analog zur Map-ClustersSidebar
  2. Document View (/documents/[docId]) ‚ÄĒ leichtgewichtig, kein
  Cluster-Management:
    - Cluster-Badge neben jedem Naming im Namings-Panel (Spalte 3)
    - Optionaler Filter: "Nur Namings aus Cluster X zeigen"
    - Kein Create/Assign hier ‚ÄĒ das geh√∂rt auf die Namings-Seite

  Die Frage an dich: Soll das Cluster-Management prim√§r auf der Namings-Seite
  leben (was konzeptuell sauber w√§re ‚ÄĒ Clustering ist eine analytische Operation
   auf Naming-Ebene, nicht auf Passage-Ebene)? Oder brauchst du es auch direkt
  beim Kodieren im Dokument?

      1047 +// Get all clusters in a project (across all maps + grounding
           + workspace)                                                  
      1048 +export async function getProjectClusters(projectId: string) {
      1049 +  return (                                                   
      1050 +    await query(                                             
      1051 +      `SELECT DISTINCT ON (n.id)                             
      1052 +         n.id, n.inscription as label,                       
      1053 +         (SELECT count(*) FROM appearances sub               
      1054 +          WHERE sub.perspective_id = n.id                    
      1055 +            AND sub.naming_id != n.id) as member_count,      
      1056 +         a.properties->>'parentMapId' as parent_map_id       
      1057 +       FROM namings n                                        
      1058 +       JOIN appearances a ON a.naming_id = n.id AND a.perspec
           +tive_id = n.id                                               
      1059 +         AND a.mode = 'perspective'                          
      1060 +       WHERE n.project_id = $1                               
      1061 +         AND n.deleted_at IS NULL                            
      1062 +         -- Exclude maps themselves (they have mapType in the
           +ir self-appearance)                                          
      1063 +         AND NOT (a.properties ? 'mapType')                  
      1064 +         -- Exclude grounding workspace                      
      1065 +         AND NOT (a.properties->>'role' = 'grounding-workspac
           +e')                                                          
      1066 +       ORDER BY n.id, n.seq`,                                
      1067 +      [projectId]                                            
      1068 +    )                                                        
      1069 +  ).rows;                                                    
      1070 +}                                                            
      1071 +                                                             
      1072 +// Get members of a cluster with their current state         
      1073 +export async function getClusterMembers(clusterId: string) { 
      1074 +  return (

      1077 +         (SELECT na.designation FROM naming_acts na          
      1078 +          WHERE na.naming_id = n.id AND na.designation IS NOT
           + NULL                                                        
      1079 +          ORDER BY na.seq DESC LIMIT 1) as designation,      
      1080 +         a.mode, a.properties                                
      1081 +       FROM appearances a                                    
      1082 +       JOIN namings n ON n.id = a.naming_id AND n.deleted_at 
           +IS NULL                                                      
      1083 +       WHERE a.perspective_id = $1                           
      1084 +         AND a.naming_id != $1                               
      1085 +       ORDER BY n.inscription`,                              
      1086 +      [clusterId]                                            
      1087 +    )                                                        
      1088 +  ).rows;

           +rojectId: string) {

           +id,

      1098 +         doc.inscription as document_label,                  
      1099 +         ann.properties                                      
      1100 +       FROM appearances member                               
      1101 +       JOIN appearances ann ON ann.directed_from = member.nam
           +ing_id                                                       
      1102 +         AND ann.valence = 'codes'                           
      1103 +       JOIN namings code ON code.id = ann.directed_from AND c
           +ode.deleted_at IS NULL                                       
      1104 +       JOIN namings doc ON doc.id = ann.directed_to AND doc.d
           +eleted_at IS NULL                                            
      1105 +       WHERE member.perspective_id = $1                      
      1106 +         AND member.naming_id != $1                          
      1107 +         AND code.project_id = $2                            
      1108 +       ORDER BY code.inscription, doc.inscription, (ann.prope
           +rties->'anchor'->>'pos0')::int`,                             
      1109 +      [clusterId, projectId]                                 
      1110 +    )                                                        
      1111 +  ).rows;

           +_id)

      1152 +    );

      1157 +       VALUES ($1, 'characterization', $2)`,                 
      1158 +      [cluster.id, researcherNamingId]

      413 +  async function clusterAction(action: string, params: Record<
          +string, any> = {}) {                                          
      414 +    const res = await fetch(`/api/projects/${data.projectId}/c
          +lusters`, {                                                   
      415 +      method: 'POST',                                         
      416 +      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },        
      417 +      body: JSON.stringify({ action, ...params })             
      418 +    });

      422 +  async function createCluster() {                            
      423 +    if (!newClusterName.trim()) return;                       
      424 +    await clusterAction('create', { inscription: newClusterNam
          +e.trim() });                                                  
      425 +    newClusterName = '';                                      
      426 +    showClusterForm = false;                                  
      427 +    const module = await import('$app/navigation');           
      428 +    module.invalidateAll();                                   
      429 +  }                                                           
      430 +                                                              
      431 +  async function selectCluster(clusterId: string) {           
      432 +    if (selectedClusterId === clusterId) {                    
      433 +      selectedClusterId = null;                               
      434 +      clusterMembers = [];                                    
      435 +      clusterPassages = [];                                   
      436 +      return;                                                 
      437 +    }                                                         
      438 +    selectedClusterId = clusterId;                            
      439 +    loadingCluster = true;                                    
      440 +    const [membersRes, passagesRes] = await Promise.all([     
      441 +      clusterAction('getMembers', { clusterId }),             
      442 +      clusterAction('getPassages', { clusterId })             
      443 +    ]);                                                       
      444 +    clusterMembers = membersRes.members || [];                
      445 +    clusterPassages = passagesRes.passages || [];             
      446 +    loadingCluster = false;                                   
      447 +  }                                                           
      448 +                                                              
      449 +  async function assignNamingToCluster(namingId: string) {    
      450 +    if (!assigningToCluster) return;                          
      451 +    await clusterAction('assign', { clusterId: assigningToClus
          +ter, namingId });                                             
      452 +    // Refresh cluster detail if viewing this cluster         
      453 +    if (selectedClusterId === assigningToCluster) {           
      454 +      await selectCluster(selectedClusterId);                 
      455 +    }                                                         
      456 +    assigningToCluster = null;                                
      457 +    const module = await import('$app/navigation');           
      458 +    module.invalidateAll();                                   
      459 +  }                                                           
      460 +                                                              
      461 +  async function removeNamingFromCluster(clusterId: string, na
          +mingId: string) {

          -h `mode = 'perspective'` that groups elements by analytical af
          -finity ‚ÄĒ Clarke's in-vivo categories (human elements, discours
          -es, political-economic forces, etc.), or categories that emerg

      224  
      225  **Pairwise interrogation** ‚ÄĒ Clarke's procedure of centering o

      320  
      321  **Discussion, not accept/reject.** When the AI produces a cue,
            the researcher does not face a binary accept/decline button. 
           Instead, they can enter dialogue *at the cue itself*: question
            the AI's reasoning, request revision, challenge the framing. 
           This discussion is a memo chain linked to the naming. A discus
           sion can result in: the AI rewriting the cue (new inscription 
           in the stack, old preserved), the AI withdrawing the cue (soft
           -delete with discussion history preserved), or the AI respondi
           ng with a deepening memo (no rewrite, but richer analytical co
           ntext).

          +thdrawn cues ‚ÄĒ so its questions emerge from the actual analyti

      277  
      278  **Documents are stored in project directories** (`projekte/{sl
           ug}/files/`), with relative paths in the database. This ensure
           s portability: a project directory contains everything needed 
           to reconstruct the project, including all media files.

      281  
      282 +Clusters are the bridge between document coding and situationa
          +l mapping. Dewey/Bentley: "Characterization develops out of cu
          +e through the **clustering** of cues and the growth of languag
          +e." Clustering IS characterization ‚ÄĒ grouping related cues and
          + naming the group is the act that moves from cue to characteri
          +zation on the CCS gradient.                                   
      283 +                                                              
      284 +**A cluster is a naming** with `mode = 'perspective'`. It has 
          +its own inscription, designation (starts at `characterization`
          +), and stack. Cluster membership is tracked in an append-only 
          +history table for full provenance.                            
      285 +                                                              
      286 +**Project-level, not map-bound.** Clusters belong to the proje
          +ct, not to a specific map. They appear automatically on any ma
          +p where at least one of their members is present. This means a
          + researcher can create clusters during coding and find them on
          + the map when they move to relational analysis.               
      287 +                                                              
      288 +**Cluster management** lives on the **Namings page** ‚ÄĒ the pri
          +vileged representation (Section 4). The right panel shows all 
          +clusters; clicking one reveals its members and all their passa
          +ges, grouped by naming and document. Namings are assigned to c
          +lusters by entering assign mode and clicking. This is an analy
          +tical operation on naming-level, not a passage-level operation
          +.                                                             
      289 +                                                              
      290 +**Cluster filter in the Document view.** The Passages panel (r
          +ight column in the document viewer) provides a cluster filter 
          +dropdown. Selecting a cluster narrows the passage list to code
          +s that belong to that cluster ‚ÄĒ enabling focused review of the
          + empirical basis for a cluster while coding.                  
      291 +                                                              
      292 +**Recursive clustering** is supported: a cluster can itself be
          + a member of another cluster. This enables multi-level analyti
          +cal organization without imposing a fixed hierarchy.

      296  Memos are the **shared inquiry medium** of the analytical proc
           ess. They capture observations, questions, tensions, and theor
           etical connections that span the research situation. In transa
           ct-qda, a memo is a first-class naming ‚ÄĒ it participates in th
           e core data model alongside entities, relations, and documents
           .
      297  
      298  **Memo creation** produces a naming with content stored in a d
           edicated `memo_content` table. Memos can be linked to any numb
           er of namings (elements, relations, silences, other memos) via
            participations. The linked elements provide analytical contex
           t: a memo about a tension between two formations links to both
           .

      311  
      312  **Memos are NOT grounding.** They document reflexive reasoning
            ‚ÄĒ CCS movement, analytical process, theoretical connections. 
           Only document anchors constitute empirical grounding. This dis
           tinction is epistemologically important: a memo about a patter
           n of silences is an analytical observation, not evidence.
      313

      314 +### 5.7 The AI Co-Researcher                                  
      315

            a **naming in the data space** ‚ÄĒ it has its own researcher-na
           ming per project, and its analytical acts (suggestions, memos,
            withdrawals) are naming acts attributed to this AI-naming. Th
           e AI is a co-actor in the analytical situation, not an instrum
           ent applied to it.
